7.2
Designers’ AI Perception
This subsection addresses the second sub-
question of the FPS, focusing on designers’
perspectives. This question is accessed from
the sample’s responses about their hopes,
concerns, and expectations regarding the
integration of gen AI into the design pro-
cess.
Without elaborating on AI, the 37 design-
ers are asked about their general perception
and attitude towards AI on a scale of one
(very negative) to ﬁve (very positive). The
consolidated answers are showcased through
a box plot in Figure 28.
Figure 28: Attitude toward AI in general among
designers in the sample.
The response data show no patterns link-
ing gender, age, profession, or AI usage
frequency with the respondents’ attitudes
toward AI. The box plot is top-heavy with
a relatively low variance, indicating a gen-
erally very positive attitude towards AI
among the designers.
This positive attitude is further represented
in the designers’ expectations of AI advan-
tages. More designers are calling AI a new
revolution, comparing AI technology with
the invention of the calculator and the com-
puter. On the other hand, four out of the
37 respondents mention establishing rules
and regulations for AI usage.
Table 5 lists advantages, while Table 6 lists
disadvantages or concerns expressed regard-
ing AI. The tables content is mentioned by
three or more designers. The count of de-
signers noting these advantages or disadvan-
tages/concerns and the percentage of the
respondents who have expressed it are dis-
played in the right column of each table.
Table 5: Designers expressed advantages.
The designers’ anticipated advantages is an
increase in eﬃciency, noted by nine out of 37
respondents. On the contrary, two respon-
dents expressed concerns about the rapid
development of AI, feeling overwhelmed and
anxious about keeping up with the progres-
sion.
Moreover, there is an expectation
that AI will tackle global challenges, ranging
from cancer treatment to autonomous ve-
hicle development and addressing environ-
mental issues. Equally emphasized is AI’s
role as a valuable search tool, widely used
for gathering information, sparking inspira-
tion, and providing collaborative support,
reducing the need to interrupt fellow stu-
dents or colleagues.
p. 41 of 80
==PAGE:44==
7.2
Designers’ AI Perception
7
DESIGNERS’ NEEDS
Table 6: Designers expressed disadvantages.
Table 6 highlights the designers’ concerns
about people becoming reliant on AI tools,
which may lead to reduced independent
thinking and loss of skills, such as writing
correct English.
This worry is as promi-
nent as concerns about copyright issues,
like replications of original artists’ work.
Besides the aspects highlighted in the two
tables, ﬁve respondents expressed concerns
about job replacement due to AI. Despite
this, the same ﬁve people expressed conﬁ-
dence about the security of their jobs, em-
phasizing the necessity for dialogue, cus-
tomer empathy, creativity, and common
sense — attributes they consider beyond
AI’s current capabilities.
This conﬁdence
is supported by their experience with cus-
tomers who frequently have unclear and
changing needs and requirements.
The designers are asked how they envi-
sion AI inﬂuencing their design process.
They are questioned di↵erently based on
the format.
Interviewees provided open-
ended responses, leading to more detailed
insights, whereas questionnaire respondents
selected from predeﬁned options on AI’s im-
pact on eﬃciency, creativity, understanding,
and decision-making, with space for addi-
tional comments. Due to the inherent di↵er-
ences in response formats, leading to vary-
ing levels of detail, the ﬁndings are pre-
sented in two distinct tables: one summa-
rizing the interview responses (Table 7) and
another for the questionnaire feedback (Ta-
ble 8). These tables highlight changes men-
tioned by at least two designers to maintain
relevance and clarity.
Table 7: Interview answers to AI’s impact on
the design process.
71% of the interviewees believe that AI will
improve eﬃciency in the design process. It
is noteworthy that they do not mention any
negative impacts. However, there is a split
in opinions about whether the introduction
of AI in design will enhance or leave quality
unchanged.
Table 8: Questionnaire answers to AI’s impact
on the design process.
As for the interview responses, Table 8 re-
veals a signiﬁcant majority, 78%, predicting
an increase in eﬃciency by introducing AI
to the design process. Unlike the interview
responses, the questionnaire results show
a strong belief in AI’s role in enhancing
creativity, with 61% of respondents high-
lighting this aspect.

Collectively, the responses reveal a positive
perception of AI’s impact on design, with
no negative impacts mentioned. Especially
regarding AI’s inﬂuence on eﬃciency, where
28 out of the 37 respondents, corresponding
to 76%, believe in AI’s potential to enhance
eﬃciency in the design process. Overall, de-
signers hold a highly optimistic view of AI’s
impact, both broadly and within the ﬁeld of
design
7.2.1
Workshop Insights
As a supplement to understanding design-
ers’ perceptions of AI and to incorporate
broader perspectives from the design indus-
try, insights from a workshop held at the
innovation consultancy IIAB are integrated
into the research.
This one-day workshop
was held in October 2023, with IIAB em-
ployees as participants, consisting of a mix
of anthropologists and designers, to address
concerns and curiosities about AI usage in
their work.
The curiosity toward AI usages includes
AI’s potential in picture generation, AI’s
potential to contribute new perspectives
in creative brainstorming and prototyping,
and AI’s ability to help with tedious work
tasks, like transcription and writing inter-
view guides, to free up time for more enjoy-
able tasks.
The concerns raised include that AI tools
might overlook important details, obser-
vations, and perspectives in research, the
trustworthiness and reliability of the tools,
the risk of becoming lazy and uncritical,
losing human touch, -understanding, and -
emotional engagement. The IIAB employ-
ees expressed fear of losing valuable collab-
orative time or having a work environment
that is too fast-paced. The biggest concern,
repeated most times, is concerns about a
drop in original thinking and the reinforce-
ment of stereotypes, leading to a loss of
valuable skills. All workshop post-its with
concerns and curiosities are shown in Appx.
05.04.
7.3
Designers’ AI Usage
To gain a comprehensive understanding of
designers’ current AI usage, the interviewees
and questionnaires are asked about which
AI tools they are utilizing. The responses
are presented in a circular diagram in Fig-
ure 29.
Figure 29: AI tools usage distribution.
The circular diagram illustrates the di-
verse AI tools designers employ, highlight-
ing ChatGPT as the most popular tool, with
97% of the respondents utilizing it — equat-
ing to all but one participant.
ChatGPT
frequently emerges in discussions about AI
during interviews, underscoring its impor-
tance and high association with AI. Follow-
ing ChatGPT, Midjourney is used by 32%
of designers, with DALL-E being employed
by 24%.
Elaborately, the designers are asked where
they know about AI tools from. A variety
of sources are mentioned, but it is primar-
ily from social media, especially through
LinkedIn, Instagram, and Facebook. This is
closely followed by word-of-mouth through
their personal and professional networks,
including family, friends, and colleagues.
News media also plays a role. While some
designers proactively seek out information
through internet searches and reading sci-
entiﬁc papers, it appears that many are not
actively searching for this knowledge but
rather coincidentally coming across it.
Subsequently, the designers are asked about
the frequency of their use of AI tools in
terms of work/study and private life on a

scale of 1 (Never or less than once a month)
to 7 (Daily). The responses are indicated
by the box plot in Figure 30.
Figure 30: AI tools usage frequencies distribu-

The answers are based on the respondents’
perception of AI tools and what they iden-
tify as AI usage.
This could range from
direct interaction with speciﬁc AI tools
like ChatGPT to indirect engagement with
AI-embedded technologies, such as smart-
phones predicting the next word in a sen-
tence or robotic vacuum cleaners. However,
the interview responses suggest a tendency
towards directly using speciﬁc AI tools.
The box plots reveal that AI is already an
integrated part of designers’ work.
It re-
veals that AI tools are used more regularly
and consistently for work or study than for
personal purposes. For work or study, the
median frequency of use is 5, corresponding
to 2–3 times per week, indicating a notable
integration in the respondent’s professional
lives.
On the other hand, the private us-
age box plot displays a wider interquartile
range, signifying a greater diversity in us-

stands at 3, equating to just 2–3 times per
month.
This variance in the interquartile
range for professional and private use evi-
dences diverse approaches and needs when
it comes to utilizing AI tools.
Respondents detail their integration of AI
into their design work.
Text-based AI
tools like ChatGPT are used for summa-
rizing texts, organizing drafts, online re-
search (googling), generating LinkedIn or
other social media content, coding, answer-
ing emails, editing text for grammar and
punctuation, translating, producing materi-

and job applications, and brainstorming.
Image-generating AI tools provides visu-
als for presentations or cover pages, and
serves as inspiration. Additionally, AI tools
are used for image editing for example to
change colors or backgrounds.
Another noteworthy remark is that most
of the interviewees expressed an interest in
a solution after explaining the aim of the
master’s study.
This emphasizes the de-
mand for developing a solution.
This section revealed an already widespread
use of gen AI among designers in their pro-
fessional activities, with AI tools being em-
ployed 2-3 times per week on average. No-
tably, among AI tools is ChatGPT, utilized
by 97% of the respondents, underlining its
signiﬁcant role.
Discovery of these tools
primarily occurs through social media and
professional networks, indicating a trend to-
wards passive rather than active seeking of
AI tools. Designers apply AI across various
tasks, from text summarization and draft
preparation to visual content creation and
editing, demonstrating AI’s varied usage po-
tential.
7.4
Need Deﬁnition
This subsection aims to capture the design-
ers’ needs by ﬁnding patterns from interview
and questionnaire insights.
The
analysis
reveals
underlying
factors
within the designers’ culture that are shap-
ing their approach to AI. Acknowledging
these factors is essential for understanding
the cultural context that a solution must
align with. These insights are displayed in
a Cultural Model [21], illustrated in Figure
31.
p. 44 of 80
==PAGE:47==
7.4
Need Deﬁnition
7
DESIGNERS’ NEEDS
Figure 31: Culture model illustrating underly-
ing external factors shaping designers’ perspec-

The model emphasizes how the designers’
AI approach is inﬂuenced by social media
both positively by creating awareness and
negatively by conveying concerns. The de-
signers are further inﬂuenced by their posi-
tion as students and/or professionals, each
with its own cultural norms regarding AI
applications.
There exists a tension be-

master the tools for beneﬁt and the ethical
considerations surrounding data security
and plagiarism avoidance. Additionally, the
inﬂuence of AI usage within their social net-

draw input and inspiration from the use
cases observed among designers in social
networks.
This social exchange enriches
their understanding and expands the scope
of possibilities for applying AI in their work.
This model is valuable for truly grasping the
underlying needs and ensuring that the pro-
posed solutions align e↵ectively with these
requirements. The identiﬁed patterns will
be encapsulated in the creation of personas,
providing a clear representation of the un-
covered user needs and preferences.
7.4.1
Key Problem Areas
This subsection seeks to identify key prob-
lem areas that a solution must align with.
These problem areas are identiﬁed through
patterns in the respondents’ answers and
are represented through three personas [6],
namely, Curious Casper, Careful Caroline,
and Dyslexic Dylan.
The personas are archetypal representations
of respondent data. These personas are not
detailed portraits of individual preferences;
instead, they function as generalized repre-
sentatives of the tendencies and key char-
acteristics identiﬁed. They serve to ensure
a user-centered perspective, keeping the ex-
pressed user behaviors and needs to remain
central to the solution development process.
The personas are detailed with names, pro-
fessions, ages, work processes, top three
preferred design programs, and top two AI
tools, and AI usage rated on a scale from 1
(never or once a month) to 5 (daily).
Curious Casper, depicted in Figure 32, is
the co-founder and CEO of a startup, thriv-
ing in a fast-paced work environment ﬁlled
with dynamic tasks. He skillfully edits prod-
uct images using Photoshop, making prod-
uct prototypes using Figma, and typically
documents his work using Miro. In his hec-
tic daily life, Casper is eager to embrace gen
AI tools, with daily use of ChatGPT for text
generation, whereas he turns to Midjourney
for creative image generation. His experi-
ence with gen AI is that it enhances his work
satisfaction by increasing eﬃciency, allow-
ing him to achieve more in less time. Casper
leverages these technologies for promptly re-
sponding to emails, conducting quick desk
research to obtain immediate information,
generating images for presentations, and
likes exploring these tools’ capabilities. De-
spite the beneﬁts, Casper often gets so eager
to apply ﬁndings and move on that he some-
times overlooks the importance of stopping
to review the output critically, potentially
missing biases or inaccuracies.

PowerPoint functionalities.

extending pictures to larger formats, and so
on. Caroline’s cautious approach may leave
her a step behind in leveraging gen AI po-
tential in her design work, such as increased
eﬃciency and enhanced creativity.
Figure 33: Persona: Careful Caroline.
Lastly is Dyslexic Dylan, visualized in Fig-
ure 34. Dylan is a design master’s student.
He uses Illustrator to make visual material
for presentation posters and uses Figma and
Miro for collaborative projects and report
documentation. Dylan has a dyslexia diag-
nosis, which challenges him in reading large
texts amount and in writing tasks. Chat-
GPT allows him to summarize text and
produce written work at a pace compara-
ble to his peers. These tasks could other-
wise consume all of his time and energy and
thus extract his focus from creative design
work. Dylan’s go-to text generator is Chat-
GPT, which he uses for all writing-related
tasks. This is, among others, due to Chat-
GPT’s capability to understand text despite
spelling and typing mistakes. Dylan faces
challenges in assessing the accuracy of AI-
generated content, which could lead to re-
liance on potentially incorrect information.
Dylan uses it daily, he is using the paid ver-
sion, allowing him to generate DALL-E im-
ages, which he uses to create front pages and
presentation images.

Dylan’s dyslexic diagnosis is included in the
collection of personas, as three interviewees
touched on the huge advantages of gen AI
when dyslexic. This perspective aligns with
the MIT study’s ﬁndings, displayed in Find-
ings 1. The MIT study found the greatest
improvement of introducing ChatGPT in
writing tasks for lower-skilled writers. This
insight underscores the potential of target-
ing lower-skilled writers in the scope. Three
key problem areas stand out from the re-
spondents’ expressed concerns and use pat-
terns:
Firstly, an overly enthusiastic ap-
proach towards AI, with uncritical AI ap-
plication across various tasks. Conversely,
there are concerns regarding data security,
skepticism towards the reliability and au-
thenticity of generated content, and copy-
right concerns, leading to a cautious ap-
proach hindering full exploration and bene-
ﬁt from these tools. The ﬁnal challenge cen-
ters on giving tasks directly to AI, without
reviewing or without the ability to assess
the accuracy; it could be practiced, for ex-
ample, by using ChatGPT to translate into
an unfamiliar language without being able
to verify the output correctness or relevance.
7.4.2
Design Ambition
The ambition of the solution is to help de-
signers get advantages of gen AI tools; to do
that, a solution must ﬁt the designers’ per-
spectives and workﬂows. With the personas
representing the designers, a solution must
balance the di↵erent needs and attitudes re-
ﬂected in the three personas, making Care-
ful Caroline feel comfortable applying AI
tools while managing Casper’s and Dylan’s
uncritical use of tools.
The insights are translated into critical re-
quirements that the solution must address
alongside criteria that are desirable for the
solution to meet. These form the founda-
tion of the solution speciﬁcation, in Table 9.
The solution speciﬁcation guides the further
development and conceptualization process.

GENERATIVE AI’S POTENTIAL IN THE DOUBLE DIAMOND
8
Generative AI’s Potential in the Double Diamond
This section’s objective is to explore and
identify potential opportunities for integra-
tion of gen AI within the double diamond
processes, targeting sub-question four of the
FPS. This exploration is based on the as-
is process as outlined in Section 2.1.2.
It
incorporates insights about gen AI’s im-
pact, detailed in Section 6. Together with
the designers’ needs’, detailed in Section 7.
Concrete gen AI potential is extracted by
analyzing gen AI’s contribution within each
double diamond step in light of the insight
from the just-mentioned sections.
Figure 35 outlines the steps observed in the
current journey. This illustration examines
the potential for integrating gen AI into
each step. As detailed in Section 2.3, the
recommendations focus on tool categories
rather than speciﬁc gen AI tools, though
examples of speciﬁc tools are provided to
illustrate their potential applications.
Figure 35: The identiﬁed steps of a double dia-
mond process.
1. Uncovering assumptions
Gen AI tools have, as well as hu-
mans, built-in cultural and user group
stereotypes from their learnings, as
discussed in Section 2.2.1. However,
this is a trait that the gen AI devel-
opers are actively striving to mitigate
due to ethical responsibilities.
This
trait is thus expected to be less and
less present over time.
To exemplify the bias in gen AI tools
and the direction in which gen AI de-
velopment is heading, Figure 36 com-
pares generated images of ’a beautiful
illustration of leadership’ with a year
gap.
The ﬁgure showcases Midjour-
ney responses from February 2023 and
DALL-E 0.2 responses from March
2024.
It had been more representa-
tive to use the same image genera-
tor. However, the Midjourney image
is an example available with an exact
prompt, whereas DALL-E is used due
to access ability.
Figure 36: AI generated images of ’a beautiful
illustration of leadership’.
The images highlight AI’s reliance on
historical data patterns, which can
lead to representations that are inac-
curate, oversimpliﬁed, or harmful to
individuals or groups.
Notably, the
February 2023 images predominantly
depict leadership as an older white
male, while the March 2024 images
include more diverse representations,
such as a female representative, and
a shift towards emphasizing the di-
rection of leadership rather than the
leader’s identity.
However, these biases are still present,
to take another example DALL-E is
once again used to generate four im-
ages showcasing ’a leader struggling
with decision-making under many un-
certainties’, showcased in Figure 37.
p. 49 of 80
==PAGE:52==
8
GENERATIVE AI’S POTENTIAL IN THE DOUBLE DIAMOND
Figure 37:
DALL-E generated images of ’a
leader struggling with decision-making under
many uncertainties’.
Even though these images are strong
emotional builders showing facial ex-
pressions, these are ﬁlled with un-
wanted historical biases, with a leader
represented
in
the
form
of
white
males, whereas one is wearing the US
ﬂag, emphasizing that this use case
can prime a project towards an un-
wanted direction.
It is not recommended to use gen AI
biases actively due to the potential
harm and the risk of cultivating his-
torical stereotypes.
Gen AI should
be used for purposes that have clear
beneﬁts rather than for creating or
spreading stereotypes. This will also
contribute to future-prooﬁng a solu-
tion as the gen AI tools are expected
to move toward bias mitigation.
2. Conducting ﬁeldwork
Gen AI has shown value for creating
initial drafts of market research, inter-
view guides, and questionnaire ques-
tions, as discussed in Section 6. This
demonstrates its value in overcoming
beginning barriers. However, employ-
ing gen AI risks reducing original-
ity and the sense of ownership over
the work.
There is a risk of over-
reliance on generated outputs, poten-
tially leading to laziness or priming of
the generated answers.
It is neces-
sary to actively and critically review
the output to ensure it will not lead
to misinformation, non-coverage of es-
sential aspects, or an output that the
designer cannot stand behind.
Using text generators for early re-
search stages can simplify complex
themes, making them easily under-
standable and e↵ectively summarizing
large amounts of text to key points to
quickly identify whether the texts are
beneﬁcial to the study and thus worth
reading. Here a big beneﬁt of gen AI
tools are that these do not get tired.
Another way to work with gen AI is to
work on a task independently before
seeking assistance from gen AI tools
to provide critical feedback, such as
helping reﬁne or add questions to a
questionnaire. Moreover, text genera-
tors can be used for fast trial and er-
ror interviews, making the generator
answer as a persona answering the in-
terview question to test if the answers
fulﬁll the interview’s intentions.
Moreover, gen AI can be beneﬁcial
for transcribing interviews through
speech-to-text generators. An exam-
ple is OpenAI’s Whisper [46], which
can produce accurate transcripts in
multiple languages despite variations
in speech pace, accents, and back-
ground noise.
While many gen AI
tools are available for transcription,
this paper does not focus on speciﬁc
alternatives, as previously argued in
Section 2.3. Utilizing AI for transcrip-
tion was a need highlighted during
the ChatGPT pilot with journalists
(Section 6.1), which is equally appli-
cable to design work. Utilizing tran-
scribing tools for interviews is partic-
ularly useful when conducting inter-
views solo, as it can be challenging
to focus on asking questions and tak-
ing notes simultaneously. These tools
allow for revisiting speciﬁc quotes or
recall responses accurately, enhancing
the quality of the research.
This analysis expects potential eﬃ-
ciency and quality gains from using
gen AI for initial drafts, fast trial and
error interviews, or interview tran-
scripts.
p. 50 of 80
==PAGE:53==
8
GENERATIVE AI’S POTENTIAL IN THE DOUBLE DIAMOND
3. Building Empathy
Using AI to build user empathy seems
almost controversial since AI does not
possess emotions nor can it empathize
with users like humans do.
It lacks
the depth of understanding, content,
or context with the nuanced insight
that comes from human perception.
While text generators can analyze
huge amounts of data from user in-
teractions, o↵ering insights into user
behavior, it is not recommended to
rely on these insights due to ethical
concerns regarding private data han-
dling and the potential for misinter-
pretation. Furthermore, AI currently
lacks the ability to read between the
lines or body language. However it is a
question of time with many AI initia-
tives to make AI capable of reading fa-
cial expression or body language. Ef-
forts like the Panoptic studio project
[17], which employs over 500 cameras
to capture human behavior and body
language, aim to teach AI systems to
interact with humans more naturally
by understanding non-verbal commu-
nication.
Even so, as AI tools currently func-
tion it is not recommended to use gen
AI tools to build user empathy. Re-
lying too heavily on AI for empathy-
related tasks might lead to a degrada-
tion in the quality of human interac-
tions and overlook human behavior’s
complex nuances What AI can con-
tribute is to create realistic user sce-
narios for bodystorming, helping de-
signers to put themselves in the user’s
environment, improving their under-
standing of user challenges and emo-
tions.
4. Identifying challenges and opportuni-
ties
Identifying challenges and opportuni-
ties involves valuable reﬂections, dis-
cussions, and analysis to map ﬁndings
meaningfully.
In this process, text generators have
shown value through interactive di-
alogues.
It is a valuable partner,
especially when working alone, con-
tributing with new perspectives, dis-
cussions, and critical thinking about
design models, resulting in a contex-
tual understanding. An example is by
questioning the placement of an ac-
tor within a stakeholder map together
with the rationale behind the posi-
tioning. Or ask for critical feedback
on a stakeholder map instead of ask-
ing it to do a stakeholder map for a
given topic. This also applies to other
methods of contributing to this step,
such as service blueprints, as-is jour-
ney maps, and user activity cycles.
Given the signiﬁcant value from re-
ﬂection and contextual placement, it
is not advised to use gen AI as an
operator for design methods.
How-
ever, it is recommended to use it as
a reﬂective sparring partner as the
true value comes from the consider-
ation and dialogue while making de-
sign models rather than the ﬁlled-out
design models themselves.
5. Synthesizing
Gen AI tools are e↵ective for identi-
fying patterns and synthesizing large
datasets of information.
They mas-
ter
organizing
data
and
generat-
ing insightful plots, diagrams, and
graphs from quantitative information.
Nonetheless, caution is advised when
analyzing qualitative data that neces-
sitates an understanding of human be-
havior, such as nuances in tone of
voice and body language in interviews.
These are crucial aspects that require
human judgment and contextual un-
derstanding.
While AI can list and
categorize data e↵ectively, reviewing
the outputs to ensure accuracy and
depth is important.
For the task of ’Identifying challenges
and opportunities, ’ the value of pat-
p. 51 of 80
==PAGE:54==
8
GENERATIVE AI’S POTENTIAL IN THE DOUBLE DIAMOND
tern recognition is not only the out-
put but also the discussions and crit-
ical thinking accompanying the pro-
cess. Therefore, it is recommended to
use gen AI as a sparing partner rather
than an operator, especially in pattern
recognition, which sets the frame for
the rest of the design process. An ef-
fective and useful use case is applying
Miro’s AI function of digitizing Post-it
notes, introducing valuable eﬃciency
to tasks that typically do not justify
the time investment.
While gen AI tools have their limita-
tions, they are recommended for syn-
thesizing and organizing quantitative
and straightforward qualitative data.
However, human reviewing is essential
for tasks demanding nuanced interpre-
tations of human behaviors.
6. Scoping
Gen AI tools have been shown to
be valuable collaborative partners for
scoping. They can contribute by re-
viewing and adding essential criteria
and requirements for solution speci-
ﬁcations and assist in drafting initial
outlines for a SOFT analysis or design
brief. Or as a helper in formulating a
strong ﬁnal problem statement from
drafts or thoughts. Moreover, image
generators can be useful to illustrate
a user pain or -needs in the project
context. This is a strong way to build
user empathy. However, this use case
is only recommended if it adds value
to the project and does not take focus.
If doing so, one must once again be
cautiously aware of the data biases so
that the solution space is not primed
in an unwanted direction.
Scoping and input often require that
the tools understand the project con-
text, so this should be done either
as part of a conversion about the
project or from a thorough description
of the project, including all relevant
thoughts behind it.
Conclusively, gen AI tools can o↵er
valuable insights for project scoping,
but their outputs must be critically re-
viewed to ensure they align with the
project’s goals and constraints. While
gen AI tools are a valuable collabora-
tive partner for this step, it is crucial
to recognize that the scoping is foun-
dational for the solution space. There-
fore, the insights provided by gen AI
tools must be met with critical and
thoughtful reviewing.
7. Ideation
Text generators can o↵er a high vol-
ume of ideas, though they often tend
to generate generic ideas. These tools
can be prompted to ideate from di↵er-
ent perspectives or roles to encourage
a broader range of creativity.
The same counts for image generators
that can o↵er diverse form variations,
as demonstrated by AI-generated im-
ages of armchairs inspired by fashion
brands created by AI designer Marco
Rambaldi in Figure 39.
Figure 38: Midjourney generated images of arm-
chairs inspired by fashion brands, created by AI
designer Marco Rambaldi.
These images can assist in inspiring
idea development and exploring form
variations.
The ability to iterative
modify constraints and make adjust-
ments within the program adds a layer
of ﬂexibility to the creative process.
However, the ﬁnished appearance of
generated images may foster a ﬁxated
view and thus limit creative explo-
ration.
The balance between time
spent in perfecting prompts for im-
age generation and the value gain is
crucial. It may be worth the time for
p. 52 of 80
==PAGE:55==
8
GENERATIVE AI’S POTENTIAL IN THE DOUBLE DIAMOND
people experienced in image genera-
tion who are quickly creating prompts.
Whereas for less experienced design-
ers, it might add more value in the
later stages of concept detailing.
Another example by Morten Rockford
Ravn illustrates 60 di↵erent variations
of a chair. This showcases image gen-
erators’ impressive potential in mak-
ing quantitative structure variations.
Although not all can, as Morten cre-
ated these in ﬁve minutes. It is a ques-
tion of time before the tools allow for
easily accessible, ﬂexible editing of the
images and thus form variations of ob-
jects. So, hopefully, this function will
soon become accessible for less expe-
rienced users as well.
Figure 39: Midjourney generated images of 60
chair variations, created by AI designer, Morten
Rockford Ravn.
Overall, gen AI is skilled at idea gen-
eration and is thus recommended to
use as an idea contributor, allowing
designers to get inspiration for fur-
ther creativity. This means using gen
AI as a tool to enrich the idea gen-
eration process, providing inspiration
rather than substituting the funda-
mental task of idea generation itself.
8. Exploration of challenges and oppor-
tunities
As already argued, much value lies in
the considerations when making de-
sign models to explore challenges and
opportunities. It is not recommended
to use AI as an operator for these
projects; instead, it should be used
as a sparing partner to discuss design
model considerations. With that said
gen AI has proved itself to be a valu-
able sparring partner, especially when
working alone.
9. Synthesizing
In synthesizing and decision-making
steps, gen AI has shown to be particu-
larly useful in prototype development.
It excels in tasks such as rapidly cre-
ating convincing context-speciﬁc pro-
totypes when the test material is not
the context itself. A concrete exam-
ple is using an AI website scraper,
such as ’html.to.design’ Figma plug-
in, making it possible to scrape web-
site material into Figma components
for a designer to work on. Gen AI al-
lows designers to create large quanti-
ties of text or visuals that ﬁt into the
prototype context without using other
people’s material.
A notable drawback is that it is clear
when something is AI generated if no
time is spent on changing the mate-
rial, as gen AI has its own style and
language. This can detract from the
authenticity or value of the material.
Still, the ability of gen AI to mini-
mize the time spent on non-essential
content creation remains a signiﬁcant
advantage, streamlining the prototype
development process and allowing for
a focus on more critical aspects of de-
sign and decision-making.
10. Reﬁning and detailing
Gen AI tools can enhance reﬁnement
and detailing, enabling the creation of
high-quality content and contributing
to more polished visual material.
Gen AI’s ability to insert realistic ele-
ments into contexts is a notable ap-
plication, e↵ectively simulating how
a concept, prototype, or idea might
p. 53 of 80
==PAGE:56==
8
GENERATIVE AI’S POTENTIAL IN THE DOUBLE DIAMOND
manifest in the real world. An exam-
ple of a tool to do so is Adobe Fire-
ﬂy [15]. The capability of these tools
makes it easier for designers to convey
their vision and the potential impact
of their designs.
Another application is gen AI CAD
makers.
An example is Leo copilot
[10] capable of making detailed part
or full CAD models for a designer to
work on from text speciﬁcations.
A
risk of using LEO is how ﬁnished its
generated material looks it can foster
a ﬁxated look and thus limit the cre-
ative imagination.
Gen AI opens up new possibilities
for designers to explore and detail
their concepts in previously diﬃcult or
time-consuming ways.
11. Evaluating
Text generators have proven valuable
in providing feedback or reviewing
work. That said, the feedback is of-
ten very positive initially, so one has
to prompt the tools to take a criti-
cal viewpoint.
It is especially good
if asked to take a speciﬁc viewpoint,
such as from a business, user, sus-
tainability, or feasibility point of view,
where it contributes with valuable an-
gles.
12. Sharing
Gen AI can o↵er insightful advice and
support for presentation and report
material.
Text generators can ad-
vise a presentation or report outline
for strong and clear communication to
strengthen the communication narra-
tive.
For
reporting,
AI
is
strong
in
proofreading,
language
reﬁnement,
rephrasing, and tone adjustment, with
speciﬁc gen AI tools tailored to do
so, like Grammarly [16]. Text gener-
ators are skilled in summarizing ex-
tensive texts, such as writing conclu-
sion drafts. Moreover, it is skilled in
writing initial drafts from fast-written
notes.
Or to provide critical feed-
back for improvement. Additionally,
AI can e↵ectively highlight key import
text paragraphs to strengthen clarity
and focus.
Regarding visuals for pitches or pre-
sentations, image generators can gen-
erate compelling and contextual im-
ages for posters or slides, enriching the
presentations.
Furthermore, gen AI
can encrypt voice clips from interviews
or provide voice clips from text quotes,
making user quotes even stronger.
Ultimately, gen AI tools are powerful
for text improvement and creating vi-
sual supplements, contributing points
that stand out strongly.
Gen AI tools can signiﬁcantly enhance
the quality of pitches, presentation
and reports.
The ﬁndings suggest that gen AI can sig-
niﬁcantly improve various design tasks in
both divergent and convergent phases of the
double diamond, particularly in areas re-
quiring rapid ideation, iteration, and pro-
totype development. However, the nuanced
understanding of human emotions and be-
haviors requires human insight, underscor-
ing the importance of using gen AI as a
collaborative tool rather than replacing cre-
ative operation and ethical judgment.
Yet, as AI technologies continue to evolve,
their applications in design will undoubt-
edly expand, pushing the boundaries of cre-
ativity and innovation.
This progression
necessitates continuous adaptation and crit-
ical evaluation of gen AI tool suggestions.
In essence, gen AI is a powerful tool for
many double diamond phases, and it’s value
is expected to grow. However, its applica-
tion must be guided by thoughtful consider-
ations, ethical responsibilities, and a blend
of AI eﬃciency with human insights.

==PAGE:57==
9
DESIGN BRIEF
9
Design Brief
This section aims to summarize the ﬁndings
from the master’s study’s problem space
into a condensed page of essential areas to
form the direction for the solution space. To
do so, this design brief [47] describes the de-
sign context, problem, aim, and limitation.
9.1
Design Context
The context for this design exploration is
grounded in the double diamond framework,
which is widely utilized across various de-
sign ﬁelds.
This framework guides pro-
cesses for products, products/services, ser-
vices, UX, UI, industrial, graphic, and other
design ﬁelds, including students and profes-
sionals in the design industry. Designers’ ex-
periences with AI vary. Essential character-
istics of design work are its user-centered ap-
proach, emphasizing the importance of iden-
tifying the correct problem, its iterative na-
ture, process adaptation, and maintaining
a holistic perspective throughout the design
journey. A double diamond process rarely
looks the same, including di↵erent models
and directions according to the tasks.
9.2
Design Problem
Gen AI is inﬂuencing almost all indus-
tries, including the design industry, creat-
ing an urgency to keep updated with de-
velopments, navigate ethical considerations,
and e↵ectively leverage gen AI beneﬁts.
The study identiﬁes three primary chal-
lenges from designers’ feedback and usage
patterns, represented by the three personas,
elaborated in Section 7.4.1:
1. An uncritical application of AI in vari-
ous tasks due to overenthusiasm (Rep-
resented by Curious Casper).
2. Data security concerns,
skepticism
about content authenticity, and copy-
right issues lead to cautious engage-
ment, which restricts exploring and
beneﬁting from gen AI (Represented
by Careful Caroline).
3. Direct task delegation to AI tools like
ChatGPT without necessary review or
accuracy assessment, combined with
concerns about tool reliability and
credibility (Represented by Dyslexic
Dylan).
9.3
Design Aim
The goal is to help designers with actionable
strategies for gen AI utilization, enhancing
the eﬃciency and quality of their work. The
solution aims to communicate meaningful
and beneﬁcial gen AI integration into de-
sign processes, taking advantage of design-
ers’ overall positive attitude towards gen AI
while communicating responsible use.
9.4
Design Limitation
The rapidly evolving nature of the gen
AI landscape presents a signiﬁcant chal-
lenge, as recommendations relevant today
may quickly become outdated within a short
time frame.
The constant introduction of
new tools o↵ering enhanced features further
complicates valuable and up-to-date guid-
ance. Additionally, a notable limitation is
the designers’ passive approach to seeking
out new gen AI tools, indicating a need for
the solution to proactively engage and in-
form the design community about best prac-
tices of gen AI applications.
p. 55 of 80
==PAGE:58==
10
CONCEPTUALIZATION
10
Conceptualization
This section dives into the study’s solution
space, focusing on idea generation and ex-
ploring potential FPS solutions. To do so,
idea generation is carried out in a structured
manner by ﬁlling out a morphology table;
hereafter, the ideas are used to create a con-
cept.
10.1
Ideation
The ideation is carried out as a co-creation
workshop with three family members (par-
ents and grandmother, respectively 69, 59,
and 84 years old), aiming to produce many
solutions emphasizing quantity over qual-
ity. A workshop setting is used as a family
visit, was already planned to use the time
e↵ectively and to bring diverse perspectives
and insights to the table. Besides facilita-
tion, participation in brainstorming sessions
ensured e↵ective time use, eliminating the
need for repeating the process. The work-
shop emerged as an eﬃcient method for
generating creative ideas.
Details of the
workshop agenda and PowerPoint slides are
available in Appendix 06.1.
In practice, idea generation is carried out
by brainstorming on means to each require-
ment listed in the ”requirement” column
of the solution speciﬁcation, as shown in
Table 9, in Section 7.4.2.
Addressing one
requirement at a time ensures a focus on
means to fulﬁll the speciﬁed function. Af-
ter each brainstorming session, ideas are
shared and documented in a morphology
table, displayed in Figure 40.
Thereafter,
ChatGPT is prompted to brainstorm solu-
tions for the same requirements to evaluate
its idea-generation capabilities and to intro-
duce additional perspectives. The morphol-
ogy table is a structured method for thor-
oughly exploring means for each solution
sub-function. The outcomes are displayed
in the morphology table, in Figure 40, and
are available in a larger format in Appendix
06.2.
After the brainstorming sessions, a group
discussion evaluated the generated ideas,
where essential means were discussed, iden-
tiﬁed, and marked with red dots in the
morphology table. Meanwhile, the limita-
tions and contradictions of crucial means
are noted in blue on the morphology table,
leading to the rejection of these means to
create viable solutions. This discussion re-
sulted in a checklist for the solution, clar-
ifying essential requirements, and incorpo-
rating key elements marked as vital (repre-
sented by red dots):
⇤Always accessible on IT devices.
⇤Provide general suggestions and con-
crete best practices.
⇤Provide an overview of categorized de-
sign methods.
⇤User-friendly layout with visual user
guidance.
⇤Communicate ethical considerations
about gen AI usage.
Considering the checklist’s constraints, in-
sights from the morphology table (Table 40)
and target personas guided the development
of ﬁve preliminary concepts, constituting a
concept catalog (Section 10.2).

10.2
Concept Catalog
The ﬁve concepts of this concept catalog
are all candidates for helping designers e↵ec-
tively enable the potential of gen AI tools.
Each concept is described through its idea
with, idea in, and di↵erence that matters [9].
The idea with deﬁnes the concept’s objec-
tive, the idea in explains how this objective
is achieved, and the di↵erence that matters
highlights its unique value proposition on
the market. Larger images of each concept
are documented in Appx. 08.
10.2.1
Concept 1, AI DesignSync
The ﬁrst concept is named ’AI DesignSync’
as it seamlessly integrates gen AI integra-
tion suggestions directly into an existing
design program. The idea with AI Design-
Sync is its appearance in designers’ current
workﬂows, making its idea in suggestions
integrated into existing design programs.
The di↵erence that matters lies in making
gen AI insights and opportunities accessible
without the need for switching between or
learning new platforms.
AI DesignSync is displayed in Figure 41,
demonstrating the integration of gen AI
knowledge into Universaldesignguide.com.
The website is chosen to demonstrate the
concept integration into an existing website,
but it is not ideal due to its narrow target of
co-creation in multidisciplinary workshops.
Yet, the platform is a familiar tool for many
design and innovation engineers, facilitating
easy proof of concept testing.

and knowledge.

of people’s everyday digital experience, ac-

of social media interaction. SoMe DesignAI
redeﬁnes how designers learn about gen AI,
Unlike traditional methods that require ac-
tively seeking information. Acknowledging
that designers are not actively seeking AI
knowledge, discovered in Section 7.3. This
concept ensures that valuable AI insights
ﬁnd their way to designers in their daily
social media ﬂows.

the potential to appeal to other employees
in design companies (besides designers) and
thus gain access to more end users.

11
Concept Detailing
This section will detail a ﬁnal MVP sugges-
tion based on analyzing the ﬁve concepts
from the concept catalog, detailed in Section
10.2. The concepts are evaluated through
the eyes of the three personas, detailed in
Section 7.4.1 and through user testing.
11.1
User Evaluation of Concepts
This section aims to evaluate the ﬁve con-
cepts through the lens of the users. There-
fore, this study examines the concepts from
the perspective of the personas and con-
ducts user testing for empirical validation.
User testing involves testing the concepts
with ﬁve design and innovation students
to collect early-stage feedback and initial
reactions to the prototypes. This analysis
results in a qualitative, user-centered as-
sessment of the concepts needed to develop
an MVP proposal.
The signiﬁcance of user testing lies in its
ability to conﬁrm that the proposed tools
are user-friendly and empower users to feel
comfortable and in control. The importance
of this testing is emphasized by Janakarajan
Akhtar, Md Haseen, and Ramkumar in AI
in Product Design [1]. Their study explains
the importance of user-centered design and
p. 61 of 80
==PAGE:64==
11.1
User Evaluation of Concepts
11
CONCEPT DETAILING
user testing to ensure that AI’s integra-
tion into design processes is welcomed and
beneﬁcial, avoiding perceptions of it being
intrusive or overwhelming.
The test provides feedback on the concepts’
communication media and presentation for-
mat. Therefore, test participants were in-
structed to focus on the overall idea rather
than the speciﬁc content. The test people
were ﬁve design and innovation students,
as the concepts are speciﬁcally targeted at
design and innovation students who are fa-
miliar with universaldesignguide.com and
the double diamond framework.
The test
follows a one-page test plan [52] detailed in
Appx. 07.1. The testing output is qualita-
tive feedback on the communication media
and content presentation formats, docu-
mented in Appx. 07.2. The responses are
summed up for each concept.
AI DesignSync
Curious Casper is working on routines and
relies heavily on his well-learned design
methods. Therefore, it is unlikely that he
will seek new design methods. He does not
look for methods or visit websites o↵ering
method overviews.
Careful Caroline values the clear presenta-
tion of potential pitfalls in AI DesignSync.
She appreciates that if such information
is available on a site she already uses, it
communicates awareness of responsible AI
tool usage. She particularly likes that the
platform advises on using the tools without
submitting personal data. However, she is
skeptical about integrating gen AI tools into
established and functional platforms, ques-
tioning the underlying motive.
Therefore,
she remains uncertain if it will convince her
to use gen AI tools.
Dyslexia Dylan appreciates the convenience
of accessing information in familiar loca-
tions where he already searches for design
methods.
The respondents recognized the value of
integrating AI DesignSync into existing
platforms, but they pointed out that the
e↵ectiveness of this approach depends on
the designers’ familiarity with one speciﬁc
platform, with no known universally used
platform.
SoMe DesignAI
Curious Casper enjoys staying updated with
the latest news about AI, even when he is
not at work. However, he misses the abil-
ity to access speciﬁc information more spo-
radically as he needs it, without scrolling
through a feed with mixed information.
Careful Caroline would not follow such a
page, as she currently lacks interest and
prefers not to mix her work and personal
life.
Dyslexia Dylan does not use LinkedIn much
since he is not a part of the job market, and
it is a very text-heavy medium. He is more
interested in how it can help him with text
tasks, whereas LinkedIn does not have or-
ganization, making it diﬃcult for Dylan to
ﬁnd the necessary tools.
Respondents view SoMe DesignAI as a valu-
able tool for outreach, e↵ectively keeping
designers informed with up-to-date general
information and news. Although the con-
tent may not delve deeply into speciﬁc de-
sign models, it’s acknowledged for creating a
sense of community among designers. Par-
ticipants appreciate the platform’s familiar
social media environment.
However, con-
cerns were raised about the credibility due
to its social media environment. Moreover,
the platform’s tendency to prioritize and
highlight recent content was noted to po-
tentially hinder users from gaining a com-
prehensive overview.

AI Design Hub
Curious Casper likes how a separate website
allows for delving into AI usage. He appre-
ciates that it’s easy to access knowledge for
a speciﬁc design method spontaneously.
Careful Caroline appreciates the empha-
sis on responsible usage, clearly delineating
the do’s and don’ts.
She believes that to
become conﬁdent with adapting gen AI, she
needs to delve deeply into its functional-
ities, which she can do with a dedicated
platform that explicitly communicates how
to use AI safely and o↵ers comprehensive
information.
Dyslexia Dylan likes the idea but doubts
that he would use it since he is already pre-
sented with many platforms in his study,
and this would be another platform on top
of those.
Respondents provided positive feedback on
AI Design Hub for its detailed and focused
approach, which provided a comprehensive
overview of design methods linked to the de-
sign process. It is appreciated for its poten-
tial to delve deeply into AI functionalities
with easily digestible content. It is only fo-
cused on gen AI usage. Designers expressed
how they could see themselves using such a
platform.
The biggest threat expressed is
that one must actively navigate to the page.
AI DesignModelMate
Curious Casper loves how AI DesignModel-
Mate can help him save time and e↵ort and
produce material quickly.
Careful Caroline expresses signiﬁcant con-
cerns regarding the concept’s dependency
on users to share data and contribute in-
formation. She feels a lack of security and
is unsure about trusting AI tools to collabo-
rate e↵ectively without compromising secu-
rity.
Dyslexia Dylan sees it as a valuable tool
that can save time and provide inputs that
he and his group might not have thought
otherwise. However, Dylan worries that the
models might seem plagiarized or unoriginal
to instructors or fellow students. Further,
the design models might end up looking like
everyone else’s, thereby losing originality if
multiple groups use AI DesignModelMate.
Respondents liked the idea of saving time
and e↵ort, along with the straightforward
approach to gen AI. Moreover, respondents
valued the visual appeal of the concept.
Nevertheless, there were signiﬁcant con-
cerns regarding data sharing, security, and
the risk of losing valuable considerations or
originality in design work.
DesignAI Academy
Curious Casper ﬁnds it diﬃcult to ﬁnd the
time to sit down and take a webinar. Casper
prefers learning the required skills when
they are needed for a given task.
Careful Caroline sees value in how a video
can ensure that designers learn a topic with-
out skipping valuable insights.
However,
she is concerned about ﬁnding time to take
webinars if they are not scheduled as part
of the work, as she strictly separates time
o↵and work hours. That said, she would
appreciate it if her workplace prioritized it.
Dyslexia Dylan likes having knowledge pre-
sented through video material, which he
typically uses for learning and seeking new
information through, e.g., YouTube. How-
ever, he is not pleased that it is yet another
platform among the many others he uses for
di↵erent purposes.
Respondents had mixed reactions to Desig-
nAI Academy’s video-based learning. While
the idea of accessible video content was fa-
vored, the commitment to watching webi-
nars and integrating this into a busy work-
ﬂow was seen as challenging.

11.2
The MVP Suggestion
This section introduces the proposed MVP,
designed to empower designers to identify
gen AI opportunities within the double di-
amond framework.
Creating an MVP di-
rectly addresses the FPS’s last sub-question.
The MVP is created based on the analysis
of the ﬁve concepts in the concept catalog,
concepts 3 and 4 emerge as the best candi-
dates, shaping the essence of the MVP.
The MVP’s purpose is clearly communi-
cated on its homepage: ”Elevate your design
process with AI as your creative partner.”
This statement stands prominently along-
side the MVP’s logo, setting a clear aim for
the user, echoing MD Haseen and Ramku-
mar’s emphasis on user-centered clarity and
control (AI for Designers, book chapter 2)
[1]. The homepage is visually represented
in Figure 52
Figure 52: MVP proposal, homepage.
Insights from concept evaluations high-
light the importance of a structured pro-
cess overview.
The MVP addresses this
by introducing a double diamond overview
with steps and methodologies, revealed by
scrolling down from the homepage.
This
overview is displayed in Figure 53.
The
overview structure draws inspiration from
concept 3, AI DesignHub, with the visual
representation inspired by the praised lay-
out in concept 4, AI DesignModelMate. The
steps and methods included are those where
gen AI integration is revealed as beneﬁcial,
these beneﬁts are elaborated in Section 8.
Figure 53: The MVP’s visual method overview.
When the mouse hovers over the various
methods, the platform reveals how AI can
integrate into them before the user clicks,
for example for ’brainstorming,’ the MVP
showcases ’Generate a large range of ideas,’
’Take di↵erent brainstorming perspectives,’
and ’Generate inspirational images.’
By
clicking, the user is navigated to a page
that o↵ers concrete, focused suggestions on
leveraging AI to enhance the design process.
This is showcased with for ’Brainstorming’
in Figure 54.
Figure 54:
MVP, wiraframes of a user click-
ing ’Brainstorming’ (See larger version in Appx.
08.6).
Concept 4, AI DesignModelMate, received
mixed feedback concerning the direct inte-
gration of gen AI in model making. While
this approach signiﬁcantly improved eﬃ-
ciency by automating model creation, it
p. 66 of 80
==PAGE:69==
12
CONCEPT EVALUATION
simultaneously removed much of the de-
signers’ control and critical engagement,
leading to a risk of uncritical acceptance of
generated outcomes.
In response, the MVP introduces a tai-
lored version of a gen AI tool, e.g., Chat-
GPT, speciﬁcally designed for distinct de-
sign tasks right next to a description of
the recommended use of the gen AI tool
and a transparent description of risks. This
approach simpliﬁes access to appropriate
AI functionalities for designers and ensures
clear communication of the tool’s capabili-
ties and limitations to help designers beneﬁt
from gen AI while keeping the designers as
the central decision-makers. The MVP does
not automatically complete design models
but enhances its use to be more of a dy-
namic partner, sparking creativity while re-
minding designers to engage critically. This
integration directly into the MVP also ad-
dresses the challenge of platform overload,
particularly beneﬁting users like Dyslexic
Dylan, who prefer to minimize the number
of platforms they engage with. The MVP
images are generated by ChatGPT 4.0 as of
March 10, 2024.
The proposed MVP is built on a combina-
tion of concepts 3 and 4, o↵ering a nuanced
solution to help designers integrate gen AI
within the double diamond framework. The
MVP addresses concrete and responsible
gen AI application suggestions, enabling de-
signers to leverage AI as a dynamic part-
ner.
The MVP is developed to enhance
the design workﬂow and ensure that design-
ers remain central to the creative process.
Hopefully contribute to a collaborative fu-
ture where designers work alongside AI as
suggested by Chignell, Wang, Zare and Li
[28] .

This section assesses the MVP’s viability
using the universal virtues framework [19],
as visualized in Figure 55.
This evalua-
tion illustrates how far the solution has
been developed. The colored areas indicate
how far each of the eight dimensions is ex-
amined, from pink (not explored) to dark
blue (thoroughly explored). Unexplored di-
mensions are elaborated with further work
within that dimension written in pink text
as the next step. Each dimension’s current
status or potential ideas (for unexplored di-
mensions) are described in black text.
The evaluation highlights how the dimen-
sions of ’need’ and ’task’ have been pri-
oritized throughout this study.
However,
fully exploring all dimensions is essential
for the MVP to evolve into a viable solu-
tion. Notably, the dimensions of ’business’
and ’strategy’ remain unexplored and re-
quire additional exploration.
Addressing
these dimensions is critical for enhancing
the MVP’s overall viability and ensuring
its success in a real-world context. Future
work should also consider engaging with
relevant stakeholders to enrich the MVP
with diverse perspectives and insights, thus
reﬁning its applicability and e↵ectiveness
in assisting designers to integrate gen AI
into their work within the double diamond
framework. An area that needs further test-
ing is ﬁnding the best approach to introduce
the MVP to users, which tackles a shared
drawback of both concepts 3 and 4. This
drawback is that users have to search for
the platform proactively.
Since the MVP
is founded on these concepts, this is also a
crucial aspect of the MVP.

13
DISCUSSION
13
Discussion
This section discusses how the master’s study answers the ﬁnal problem statement’s (FPS)
sub-questions, culminating in creating a minimum viable prototype (MVP).
The master’s initial purpose was to answer the research question ’How might we help de-
signers integrate and beneﬁt from generative AI in the design process?’. A combination of
the extent of this question and the study’s limited time frame leads to a reevaluation of the
research question to an FPS: How might we create an MVP of a solution that helps designers
identify gen AI opportunities within the double diamond framework?
The selection to focus on the double diamond is due to its widespread recognition, the
author’s familiarity, and its clear visual communication of converging and diverging phases.
The decision to focus on a single design framework comes from the insight, detailed in Section
2.1.1, that tasks and methods highly align across various design frameworks. This analysis
identiﬁed four key principles common to design frameworks: 1. a user-centered approach,
2. identifying the root problem, 3. iterating, and 4. holistic thinking. This underscores the
potential applicability of the MVP to designers with di↵erent design processes.
The FPS sub-questions are listed, along with how they are carried out and their results,
which contribute to answering the FPS, with the results written in blue text.
1. What are typical steps and design methods of a double diamond process?
The typical design steps and methods are identiﬁed in Section 2.1.2 through an analysis
of 14 completed double diamond processes.
Multiple steps are identiﬁed for each double diamond phase. In the problem space’s
diverging phase, typical steps include uncovering assumptions, conducting ﬁeldwork,
building empathy, and identifying challenges and opportunities. The convergence phase
focuses on synthesizing and scoping.
In the solution space, diverging steps involve
ideation and further exploration of challenges and opportunities, while converging steps
in the solution space include synthesizing, reﬁning, detailing, evaluating, and sharing.
The steps map out the designer’s journey and are used to identify gen AI opportunities.
The design methods helping to fulﬁll these steps are detailed in Section 2.1.2 Figure 9.
2. What are designers’ perspectives on AI, including hopes and concerns?
Designers’ perspectives on AI are examined by analyzing insights from 14 interviews
and 23 questionnaires, engaging a total of 37 designers from di↵erent design ﬁelds. The
respondent provides a broad view of designers’ processes and their expectations, hopes,
and concerns regarding gen AI integration.
Designers’ gen AI perspectives are overall optimistic. Their hopes highlight potential
beneﬁts such as enhanced eﬃciency, the ability to tackle challenges, robust search ca-
pabilities, strong brainstorming tools, and reduced tedious tasks. Designers believe
that gen AI will both increase design process eﬃciency and creativity. However, de-
signers express ethical concerns about reduced independent thought, the absence of
clear copyright and ownership guidelines, data privacy issues, and the risk of becoming
over reliant on gen AI tools. The insights underscore the importance of adopting a
balanced approach to introducing gen AI, maximizing its advantages while addressing
potential drawbacks.
Building on designers’ optimistic yet cautious perspectives on AI, a study by Deloitte
(October, 2023) [5] on gen AI’s role in business value creation echoes the need for
p. 69 of 80
==PAGE:72==
13
DISCUSSION
strategic integration within the design process. Deloitte’s study analyses over 4600
companies. The study shows how strategic integration of gen AI is essential for en-
hancing market value and competitive advantage. It highlights gen AI’s transformative
potential as a key factor for future business success, emphasizing the value of purpose-
ful integration of gen AI. This study demonstrates the broader impact of strategic AI
integration beyond the design ﬁeld. In essence, the ﬁndings from the Deloitte study
validate and enrich the master’s study, providing a comprehensive framework for under-
standing the strategic signiﬁcance of gen AI in achieving value creation and sustaining
organizational growth in the digital age.
3. What potential impact do text generators have on productivity and quality
when applied to sub-tasks? Text generators’ potential impact on productivity and
quality is assessed by experimenting with ChatGPT 4.0, serving as a representative
example of a text-generating tool. The analysis in Section 6.1 includes a pilot study
that aims to replicate the signiﬁcant e↵ects of ChatGPT on writing tasks, as identiﬁed
in an MIT study [38], focusing on the journalism sector.
Alongside this pilot, the
study also examines ChatGPT 4.0’s inﬂuence on various design methods implemented
throughout the master’s research process, as discussed in Section 6.2.
Text generators can signiﬁcantly boost design eﬃciency and innovation by streamlining
initial drafts, reducing tedious tasks, and fostering idea generation. However, its use
requires careful ethical consideration and critical assessment to maintain originality
and depth in the design process.
The transformative potential of gen AI within the design process, as explored, echoes
the ﬁndings of Regenwetter et al. (2022) [49], who discuss the strategic use of deep
generative models in engineering design tasks like topology optimization and shape
synthesis. Both studies underscore AI’s revolutionary potential to transform design
by enabling more eﬃcient, innovative, and customized solutions. These also highlight
the importance of a balanced approach to AI integration, emphasizing the enhance-
ment of the design process while addressing ethical and practical challenges.
This
master’s study and the study by Regenwetter et al. (2022) collectively advocates for
the thoughtful integration of gen AI in design to unlock new levels of innovation while
ensuring ethical and practical considerations and human-centered design.
4. Where within the double diamond framework do opportunities for inte-
grating gen AI lie? To identify opportunity spaces for gen AI integration within the
double diamond, the study reviews and analyses the insights from the analysis of the
double diamond steps, designers’ AI perspectives, and the impact of text generators.
The ﬁndings are synthesized to speciﬁc areas within the design process where gen AI
provides value, as this is identiﬁed as the gap in the current state of studies, Section
3. It is documented in Section 8, showing the identiﬁcation of potential use cases for
gen AI integration within the double diamond while considering the limitations.
Opportunities for integrating gen AI within the double diamond framework lie across
all its phases; discover, deﬁne, develop, and deliver. In the discover phase, gen AI
potential lies in conducting ﬁeldwork and assists in identifying challenges and oppor-
tunities. In deﬁne, it can assist in synthesizing and scoping; in develop, it supports
ideation and exploration of challenges and opportunities; and in the deliver phase, it
enhances reﬁning and detailing, synthesizing, evaluating, and sharing design outcomes.
Identifying where within the double diamond opportunities for gen AI integration lie
was a critical process step, highlighting the potential of gen AI tools in a wide range
of design activities.
p. 70 of 80
==PAGE:73==
13
DISCUSSION
5. How can gen AI opportunities e↵ectively be communicated to designers -
what are e↵ective media to do so? To explore how the identiﬁed gen AI opportu-
nities can be e↵ectively communicated to designers, the study develops and evaluates
various concept prototypes across di↵erent media, showcasing the content in di↵erent
ways. These are detailed in Section 10. These media are selected based on their rel-
evance to end-users and evaluated through the personas and early-stage user testing
with ﬁve design and innovation students, detailed in Section 11.
To e↵ectively communicate gen AI opportunities to designers, the most successful me-
dia is identiﬁed as an online platform that can be accessed spontaneously everywhere
with an internet connection. The MVP must provide a visual overview of categorized
design methods according to double diamond steps. It must o↵er general suggestions
and concrete best practices to the designers, with clear, curated, and accessible in-
formation that encourages responsible use.
Moreover, the research emphasized the
importance of a visual and interactive solution. Based on the analysis of user feed-
back and persona evaluation, a combination of dedicated platforms like concept 3 AI
DesignHub, which o↵ers deep dives into AI functionalities, and concept 4 AI Design-
ModelMate, which streamlines design tasks through automation, emerges as promising
solutions. These platforms o↵er a balance of spontaneity and depth, allowing design-
ers to access AI tools and knowledge organically within their workﬂows without the
burden of seeking out information or committing to lengthy learning sessions.
6. What is an MVP for a solution helping designers identify gen AI opportuni-
ties within the double diamond framework? This sub-question directly points to
the study’s output: The development of an MVP helping designers in identifying gen
AI opportunities within the double diamond framework. The MVP’s creation builds
on a cumulative of study insights, incorporating speciﬁc application recommendations
and the most e↵ective communication media informed by feedback gathered from ini-
tial concept evaluation, ensuring that the ﬁnal product is both practical and aligned
with the designers’ needs.
The MVP for a solution helping designers identify gen AI opportunities within the
double diamond framework is a user centered online platform o↵ering structured guid-
ance. The MVP clearly communicated its purpose of enhancing the design process
with AI as a creative partner, ensuring clarity and control for the user. Focusing on
visual representation and easy navigation, it provides a comprehensive overview of the
double diamond framework, highlighting steps and methodologies where AI integration
can be beneﬁcial. This guidance includes concrete use suggestions for e↵ective use of
gen AI. The platform includes integrated, tailored versions of gen AI tools, like Chat-
GPT, for speciﬁc design tasks while maintaining designers’ critical engagement and
decision-making. This approach addresses both the eﬃciency and creativity needs in
design work, making it a tool for designers to explore and apply gen AI opportunities
within their existing processes.
In conclusion, this study provides an understanding of how gen AI can be integrated into
the design process, addressing both the potential beneﬁts and the challenges. The proposed
MVP and the insights into e↵ective communication strategies o↵er a solid foundation for
designers to get advantages of gen AI’s capabilities, ensuring that they remain at the fore-
front of technological advancements. The journey through the double diamond framework,
enriched with gen AI, promises a future where design processes are more eﬃcient, creative,
and innovative.
p. 71 of 80
==PAGE:74==
13.1
Study Limitations
13
DISCUSSION
A relevant question is what lies ahead for gen AI within the design ﬁeld. The DMEXCO
Content Team discusses the transformative potential of gen AI within the creative and de-
sign industries (December 14, 2023) [51].
This paper predicts signiﬁcant breakthroughs
in creative tasks such as design problem-solving, with time-saving beneﬁts and enhanced
creativity. Similarly, the document by Twoday (June 28, 2023) [12] underscores gen AI’s
evolution from speciﬁc problem-solving to creating art, optimizing business processes, ana-
lyzing customer data to tailor product designs, and automating tasks to boost eﬃciency and
create customized content, improving the user experiences. The paper describes how gen
AI can take over repetitive tasks, freeing up time and resources for creative and innovative
tasks if learning to balance human-computer interaction.
Bernard Marr (May 31, 2023) [29] discusses the future of gen AI beyond applications like
ChatGPT and Stable Di↵usion, highlighting its expanding inﬂuence across multiple sectors.
Marr’s analysis predicts a future where gen AI signiﬁcantly deepens its integration, enhanc-
ing both productivity and creativity. Marr foresees language models gaining a better grasp
of human psychology and creativity, leading to better textual content. He predicts similar
advancements for visual generators, creating realistic images, videos, and 3D models. His
paper highlights how gen AI will streamline product design development by optimizing ma-
terials and engineering. Marr emphasizes that gen AI’s role in innovation requires a balanced
approach, considering ethical implications to get its potential and tackle upcoming challenges
fully.
These predictions underscore the importance of strategically integrating gen AI within the
design process, echoing the need for a balanced approach that enhances creativity and eﬃ-
ciency while addressing ethical considerations.
13.1
Study Limitations
Limited time availability has necessitated assumptions, displayed in Table 11, along with
evaluating their potential impact on the MVP’s robustness if they prove inaccurate and the
study’s approaches to mitigate risks associated with the assumptions made.

evolving ﬁeld, ensuring relevance and insight into the future
potential of text generation technology. Even with the
caution, the impact is considered high due to the rapidly
evolving ﬁeld of gen AI cf. 2.2.2.

demonstrated e↵ectiveness in those instances. Yet, as the
analysis draws from an analysis of 14 double diamond
processes involving various designers, the extracted steps and
methods are considered to provide a reliable foundation.
Moreover, the MVP guides the double diamond framework
through steps, phases, and methods. This ensures the MVP’s
relevance and utility, even if speciﬁc steps do not align with a
designer’s.
Table 11: Summary of assumptions made for the master’s study.
This table outlines the study’s limitations, together with the potential impact of each as-
sumption made. For further development, it is important to focus on the assumptions with
the highest impact on the MVP’s robustness. The highest threat to the MVP is identiﬁed
as the rapidly evolving nature of the gen AI ﬁeld, necessitating continuous adaption of the
MVP.
13.2
Future Work
Reﬂecting on the study’s ﬁndings, this section identiﬁes areas for future work. A notice-
able area lies in continuously developing the Minimum Viable Prototype (MVP) towards a
working Minimum Viable Product (MVP). Key steps for further work toward an MVP are
identiﬁed in the concept evaluation (Section 12), suggesting a path forward, emphasizing the
need for further testing and validation to ensure the MVP’s relevance and utility in design
practices.
Further steps involve potential collaboration with design educational institutions, such as ex-
ploring partnerships with DTU’s Design and Innovation program and/or DTU’s AI board.
This collaboration aims to integrate the MVP into education, enhancing AI literacy among
design students.
The rapidly changing nature of the gen AI ﬁeld presents a signiﬁcant challenge to the MVP’s
relevance over time (c.f. Table 11). A proactive approach to this challenge could involve
integrating the MVP into an educational course and making updating the MVP a part of
the course material. It could also be a job managed by teaching assistants who can observe
its usage among students and update the MVP accordingly. This method would provide
p. 74 of 80
==PAGE:77==
14
REFLECTION
valuable, ongoing feedback and ensure the MVP updates alongside evolving design practices
and technological advancements, maintaining its utility and relevance.
Moreover, a future step lies in programming the website and creating ﬁne-tuned gen AI mod-
els. This is necessary to tailor the MVP’s capabilities to speciﬁc design contexts, enhancing
its applicability and e↵ectiveness.
Another interesting study would be replicating the promising results of the ChatGPT pilot
study analyzing ChatGPT’s impact within journalism (Section 6.1), but instead within de-
sign work. A study similar to the journalism pilot can be conducted to explore the impact
of ChatGPT on various design tasks; this could be done within design ﬁelds such as a design
consultancy, product design company, graphic design house, or even design sprints. In such
a study, the content creation process can be divided into the steps identiﬁed in the as-is
journey, in Section 2.1.2, to investigate the changes in time allocation for di↵erent tasks.
This proposed study would compare design workﬂows with and without ChatGPT integra-
tion. Data to assess the changes would include self-assessment surveys and observations by
at least ﬁve observers. Five observers are experienced as the minimum number of observers
through the Journaslm pilot. This exploration would contribute to a deeper understanding
of gen AI’s impact on the design process.
14
Reﬂection
Reﬂecting on the project, the initial expectation was a deep dive into exploring and un-
derstanding gen AI tools, envisioning multiple MVP user test iterations. Yet, due to the
discovered task’s complexity, the scope quickly shifted focus toward ChatGPT and its ap-
plication within the double diamond framework.
Few processes ran smoothly, but this project faced challenges from the beginning, starting
in a hospital bed with both typhoid and dengue fever obtained during summer vacation.
Further complications arose with personal challenges, a throat infection, and, in addition, a
change in supervisor late in the project’s progress due to illness. Despite these hurdles and
with a six-week project extension, the study successfully reached completion, answering the
FPS and its sub-questions.
Looking retrospectively, if given another opportunity to do the task over, the study should
have started with a thorough literature research, ideally as a course before the master’s
study, to create a solid foundational groundwork. Moreover, choosing a narrower project
scope from the beginning had been beneﬁcial. A more narrow scope might have helped the
study advance, focusing either on students or professional life, on the impact of AI in the
design process, or on developing e↵ective communication for updates and solutions. Gener-
ally, the thesis time frame was overestimated. Formulating the project objectives prior to
the project’s start would have allowed for a more focused approach.
Had the study been revisited, collaboration work with a teammate would have been pre-
ferred. Solo work involves numerous hours of independent work and decision-making, which
has been challenging, given the author’s social nature. To mitigate feelings of isolation, brain-
storming sessions with family and sharing with friends in social settings became a strategy
p. 75 of 80
==PAGE:78==
15
CONCLUSION
to beneﬁt collective insights and perspectives. Moreover, it became a strategy to work with
ChatGPT and ask ChatGPT for sparring.
Completing this study has signiﬁcantly broadened my understanding of gen AI tools, which
I had barely used before. The ChatGPT pilot study (Section 6.1), in particular, opened my
eyes to the promising impact and capabilities of gen AI. I am convinced that the knowledge
I have gained will have an impact on my upcoming projects as I plan to incorporate gen AI
tools. I believe that this AI collaboration will allow me to streamline tedious tasks, such
as creating stock videos, fast drafts, or sourcing freely usable images, but also require more
time allocated to critically review and adapt the generated content. I can conﬁdently state
that this study has made me a stronger, more capable designer, thanks to gen AI.
15
Conclusion
This master’s study aims to improve understanding of how generative AI can be incorporated
into the double diamond framework. Despite designers’ optimistic view on the integration of
generative AI to revolutionize design practices by enhancing creativity and eﬃciency, con-
cerns regarding ethical use and over-reliance remain. The study explores how to integrate
generative AI in the double diamond framework culminating in the creation of a minimum vi-
able prototype that communicates responsible and e↵ective generative AI usage to designers.
The prototype presents a user-centered online platform. It features an overview of the dou-
ble diamond process, including methods where generative AI proves advantageous. Upon
selecting a method, the prototype o↵ers detailed, method-speciﬁc recommendations together
with an integration window. This window features a customized generative AI tailored to
provide targeted assistance for the chosen method.
Future work for this research includes reﬁning and integrating the prototype. The goal is
to ensure that designers have the necessary knowledge and skills to use AI. This research
contributes to a responsible, innovative, and AI-powered design culture.
